Detailed characterisation of known systems is important for informing and testing models. The hot Jupiter <jats:italic>\u03c4</jats:italic> Boo Ab orbits the primary star in the long-period (<jats:italic>P</jats:italic> \u2273 1000 yr), highly eccentric (<jats:italic>e</jats:italic> ~ 0.9) double star system <jats:italic>\u03c4</jats:italic> Bo\u00f6tis. Due to the long orbital period, the orbit of the stellar binary is poorly constrained.</jats:p>\n<jats:p><jats:italic>Aims.</jats:italic> Here we aim to constrain the orbit of the stellar binary <jats:italic>\u03c4</jats:italic> Boo AB in order to investigate the formation and migration history of the system. The mutual orbital inclination of the stellar companion and the hot Jupiter has important implications for planet migration. The binary eccentricity and periastron distance are important for understanding the conditions under which <jats:italic>\u03c4</jats:italic> Boo Ab formed.</jats:p>\n<jats:p><jats:italic>Methods.</jats:italic> We combine more than 150 yr of astrometric data with twenty-five years of high-precision radial velocities. The combination of sky-projected and line-of-sight measurements places tight constraints on the orbital inclination, eccentricity, and periastron distance of <jats:italic>\u03c4</jats:italic> Boo AB.</jats:p>\n<jats:p><jats:italic>Results.</jats:italic> We determine the orbit of <jats:italic>\u03c4</jats:italic> Boo B and find an orbital inclination of \n47.2<jats:sub>\u22123.7</jats:sub><jats:sup>+2.7</jats:sup>\n\u00b0, a periastron distance of \n28.3<jats:sub>\u22123.0</jats:sub><jats:sup>+2.3</jats:sup>\n au, and an eccentricity of \n0.87<jats:sub>\u22120.03</jats:sub><jats:sup>+0.04</jats:sup>\n. We find that the orbital inclinations of <jats:italic>\u03c4</jats:italic> Boo Ab and <jats:italic>\u03c4</jats:italic> Boo B, as well as the stellar spin-axis of <jats:italic>\u03c4</jats:italic> Boo A coincide at ~45\u00b0, a result consistent with the assumption of a well-aligned, coplanar system.</jats:p>\n<jats:p><jats:italic>Conclusions.</jats:italic> The likely aligned, coplanar configuration suggests planetary migration within a well-aligned protoplanetary disc. Due to the high eccentricity and small periastron distance of <jats:italic>\u03c4</jats:italic> Boo B, the protoplanetary disc was tidally truncated at \u22486 au. We suggest that <jats:italic>\u03c4</jats:italic> Boo Ab formed near the edge of the truncated disc and migrated inwards with high eccentricity due to spiral waves generated by the stellar companion.</jats:p>", "DOI": "10.1051/0004-6361/201834368", "type": "journal-article", "created": {"date-parts": [[2019, 4, 19]], "date-time": "2019-04-19T11:51:12Z", "timestamp": 1555674672000}, "page": "A59", "source": "Crossref", "is-referenced-by-count": 0, "title": ["Constraining the orbit of the planet-hosting binary \u03c4 Bo\u00f6tis"], "prefix": "10.1051", "volume": "625", "author": [{"ORCID": "http://orcid.org/0000-0002-0174-2466", "authenticated-orcid": false, "given": "A.
